# Sample Report - AT&T Syslog Analytics v1.1
Patricio Villar  
September 29th 2016  

## Index

* Tidy Data
* Event Top 25
* Node Top 10
* Network Event Rating
* L2 Stability: Mining SPT Events
* L3 Stability. Mining Routing Events

*********

## Tidy Data:

The principles of tidy data provide a standard way to organise data values within a dataset. A standard makes initial data cleaning easier because you don't need to start from scratch and reinvent the wheel every time. The tidy data standard has been designed to facilitate initial exploration and analysis of the data, and to simplify the development of data analysis tools that work well together. Current tools often require translation. You have to spend time munging the output from one tool so you can input it into another. Tidy datasets and tidy tools work hand in hand to make data analysis easier, allowing you to focus on the interesting domain problem, not on the uninteresting logistics of data.
Syslog Data doesn't comply with Tidy Data standards, so data indexing is required for every single type of syslog to be analyzed. In this particular example, we are indexing 24 hours (~800Mb) of Cisco-formatted Syslog data.
For more info, read Wickham's paper about this topic: 

https://www.jstatsoft.org/article/view/v059i10




### Event Top 25:

Top Events mining allows to quickly identify which events are persistent and recurrent in the analyzed environment. When grouped by severity, it makes easier to focus in Emergency Errors, if any. This might not lead to architecture insights, but in the long term it will certainly help to depure and make the log datastore cleaner:

","marker":{"fillcolor":"rgba(140,86,75,1)","color":"rgba(140,86,75,1)","line":{"color":"transparent"}},"xaxis":"x","yaxis":"y"}]},"evals":[]}</script><!--/html_preserve-->

Conclusions: 

* SNMPD Errors are triggering more than 30% of the network events, this is due to a device with improper SNMPv3 credentials trying to access a range of network devices. Also, improper device discovery, as this same rogue poller tried to discover an entire 6500 chassis (more than 15000 SNMP variables/objects)
* Improper set up of WCCP redirection in Internet border switches is contributing in another 10% of network logs.

### Host Top 10:

Top Hosts mining allows to quickly identify which hosts contribute the most with the log datastore. Log data may vary in its distribution, but at the end we should have a "normalized" cumulative distribution function of events among every network node.

Conclusions: 

* As usual, access nodes are the ones that concentrate the highest amount of events. However, this is due to the abnormal situation of flapping ports, which should be solved by the operations team.
* Improper set up of WCCP redirection in Internet border switches is contributing in another 10% of network logs.
* These TOP 10 Nodes concentrate %38.5 percent of the total amount of network events. By solving these issues log storage space and report processing time could be reduce in 40% and 50% respectively.


###Event Rating

Event Rating is an approach to solve multiple network events/issues in fewer actions by applying Pareto's analysis. The rating algorithm considers affected hosts count and severity; so by solving big bubbles first one eliminates higher-risk scenarios first.

Conclusions: 

* There are critical CPU alerts for 1 Node, as CPURising Threshold is being exceeded. This might lead to a capacity re-analysis.
* There are critical Power alerts for 1 Node. Operations should review this item.
* There are 3 Hosts reporting Individual Port-Channel ports flapping.
* There are Catalyst redundacy events (VSS sync).
* There are Nexus VPC redundancy events.
* There are SPT events to be investigated further in the next section.

### L2 Stability Analysis: Mining SPT Events

L2 Stability analysis is a tool that allows the NA to identify/detect different situations, namely:

* Network isn't reacting as designed, when a specific event occurs.
* STM state machine remains in an undefined state (network not able to converge by itself)
* L2 Domain isn't properly secured.

<script type="application/json" data-for="htmlwidget-4790">{"x":{"layout":{"margin":{"b":150,"l":50,"t":100,"r":50,"pad":4},"title":"SPT Active/Unstable Nodes","showlegend":true,"xaxis":{"domain":[0,1],"title":"SPT Event Ratio | Node","showgrid":false,"zeroline":false,"showticklabels":false},"yaxis":{"domain":[0,1],"showgrid":false,"zeroline":false,"showticklabels":false}},"config":{"modeBarButtonsToRemove":["sendDataToCloud"]},"base_url":"https://plot.ly","source":"A","data":[{"hole":0.6,"labels":["172.19.2.5","usto29dcrtn-serv1-sw","usto38dcrtn-serv1-sw"],"values":[213,455,471],"name":"SPT Unstable Nodes","type":"pie","marker":{"fillcolor":"rgba(31,119,180,1)","color":"rgba(31,119,180,1)","line":{"color":"transparent"}}}]},"evals":[]}</script><!--/html_preserve-->

Conclusions: 

* There are nodes (servers) connected to server access switches performing L2 bridging. This leads to recurring SPT loops. The NA should analyze whether the L2 domain is properly secured or not (verify that L2 bulletproof best practices are applied).


### L3 Stability: Mining Routing Events

L3 Stability analysis is a tool that allows the NA to identify/detect different situations, namely:

* Network Routing isn't reacting as designed, when a specific event occurs.
* Routing Protocols present a recurring pattern of events (network not able to converge by itself, i.e.   routing loops)
* Routing domain boundaries and security.

Conclusions:

* EGP (BGP) and IGP events where identified during this analysis.
* IGP events occured due to the failure of physical elements and the network properly recovered by itself.
* Some BGP events ocurred due to network glitchs in one WAN provider (BFD in charge of fast detection). These events are recurrent, so the client may want to review this situation with the service owner.
